8:["$","blockquote",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["The camera is the ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"matter"}],". 9:["$","p",null,{"children":["It is deliberately ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"not"}]," an audio visualizer, and ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"not"}]," a camera filter. The camera (or, when it is off, a procedural source) is the ",["$","em",null,{"children":"primary"}]," visual material — it gets carried along the chaotic curve, aged, pixelated and dissolved."]}]
a:["$","p",null,{"children":["And there is a quieter idea underneath. Because the camera always faces ",["$","em",null,{"children":"you"}],", ",["$","em",null,{"children":"you"}]," are the matter — your face, your room, fed in as one more initial condition of a chaotic system. It is a small lesson in two halves. On one side, ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"responsibility"}],": what the piece becomes is made out of what you choose to put in front of it. On the other, the reminder that ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"it exceeds you"}]," — this is the butterfly effect, so the same gesture never lands twice, and you can never quite predict, let alone steer, where the chaos carries your reflection. You are unmistakably ",["$","em",null,{"children":"part of"}]," the system and just as unmistakably not in control of it. If you have lived through a heat wave wondering how we got here, that double bind will feel familiar."]}]

c:["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Everything runs on-device."}]," The video feed never leaves your phone — no upload, no backend, no tracking."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Camera and audio are optional, and motion is never required."}]," Deny the camera and the piece still works (a procedural source takes over). Mute the music and the visuals keep moving. Ignore the touch gestures and the system still breathes on its own."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"No raw values, ever."}]," Touch input and audio are always smoothed before they reach a shader or a parameter — chaos is wild enough without feeding it jitter."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"No WebGL fallback."}]," No WebGPU means a clean “unsupported” screen, not a degraded experience."]}],"\n"]}]
d:["$","h2",null,{"children":"Lorenz, 1963: deterministic chaos in three equations"}]
e:["$","p",null,{"children":"A bit of history, because it makes the rest taste better."}]
f:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Edward Norton Lorenz"}]," (1917–2008) was a meteorologist and mathematician at MIT. Starting from Barry Saltzman’s equations for thermal convection, he reduced the problem to ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"three coupled ordinary differential equations"}]," and published ",["$","a",null,{"href":"https://journals.ametsoc.org/view/journals/atsc/20/2/1520-0469_1963_020_0130_dnf_2_0_co_2.xml","children":["$","em",null,{"children":"Deterministic Nonperiodic Flow"}]}]," in 1963 — one of the most cited papers in the field."]}]
10:["$","p",null,{"children":["The legend is real: two years earlier, re-running a weather simulation on a Royal McBee LGP-30, Lorenz re-entered a value as ",["$","code",null,{"children":"0.506"}]," instead of the stored ",["$","code",null,{"children":"0.506127"}],". The forecast diverged completely. A rounding error in the fourth decimal had rewritten the weather. That is ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"sensitive dependence on initial conditions"}]," — later nicknamed the ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"butterfly effect"}],", after his 1972 talk ",["$","em",null,{"children":"“Does the flap of a butterfly’s wings in Brazil set off a tornado in Texas?”"}]," (The attractor even ",["$","em",null,{"children":"looks"}]," like a butterfly, which never hurt the branding.)"]}]
11:["$","p",null,{"children":["What makes the Lorenz attractor ",["$","em",null,{"children":"strange"}],": the trajectory is ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"bounded"}]," (it never escapes), ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"never periodic"}]," (it never repeats), ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"never self-intersecting"}],", and it lives on a ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"fractal"}]," of non-integer (Hausdorff) dimension ≈ 2.06. The system is ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"dissipative"}]," — phase-space volumes contract at a constant rate, the divergence of the field being a negative constant — and yet trajectories are chaotic: everything collapses onto a zero-volume fractal, while two neighbouring paths pull apart exponentially. The rate of that pulling-apart has a number — the largest ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Lyapunov exponent"}],", about ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"0.906"}]," at the canonical parameters — and it is exactly how fast the butterfly effect compounds: a tiny error doubles roughly every three-quarters of a time unit, until all prediction is lost."]}]
12:["$","aside",null,{"className":"my-6 rounded-md border p-4 text-sm leading-6 border-blue-500/30 bg-blue-500/5","children":[["$","p",null,{"className":"mb-2 font-semibold text-foreground","children":"The parameters are physics, not magic numbers"}],["$","div",null,{"className":"[&>:first-child]:mt-0 [&>:last-child]:mb-0","children":[["$","p",null,{"children":"In the convection model the three constants mean something concrete:"}],["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"σ (sigma)"}]," is the ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Prandtl number"}]," — momentum diffusivity over thermal diffusivity."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"ρ (rho)"}]," is a normalized ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Rayleigh number"}]," — essentially ",["$","em",null,{"children":"how hard you are heating from below"}],". Below a critical value near 24.74 the flow settles; above it, chaos. The classic ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"ρ = 28"}]," sits comfortably in the chaotic regime."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"β (beta)"}]," is a geometric factor tied to the aspect ratio of the convection rolls."]}],"\n"]}],["$","p",null,{"children":"So the app’s “intensity” knob is literally a thermostat. Fitting, for something born in a heat wave."}]]}]]}]
13:["$","p",null,{"children":["And you can ",["$","em",null,{"children":"watch"}]," a system cross into chaos by turning that thermostat. Hold σ and β at their canonical values and sweep ρ: at ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"ρ = 14"}]," the flow spirals calmly into a fixed point and stays there; nudge it to ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"ρ ≈ 24"}],", just under the threshold, and it teeters — long, wandering transients that almost settle but don’t; at ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"ρ = 28"}]," it never settles again. Same three equations, one number hotter."]}]
14:["$","$L3",null,{"lightSrc":"/images/2026/lorenz-clash/rho-triptych.webp","darkSrc":"/images/2026/lorenz-clash/rho-triptych.webp","alt":"Three Lorenz trajectories side by side at rho = 14 (spiralling into a fixed point), rho = 24 (long transient on the edge of chaos) and rho = 28 (the full strange attractor).","width":1672,"height":941}]
15:["$","p",null,{"children":["And it still matters. Lorenz’s result is ",["$","em",null,{"children":"why"}]," weather is only predictable about two weeks out, and it is the reason modern forecasting is done as ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"ensembles"}]," — run many slightly-perturbed initial states and forecast the ",["$","em",null,{"children":"distribution"}],", not a single line. The same idea separates ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"weather"}]," (a chaotic spell of heat) from ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"climate"}]," (the baseline quietly shifting underneath). Beyond meteorology, the Lorenz system shows up in nonlinear electronics, population biology, secure communication via chaos synchronization, and a lot of generative art — including this one."]}]

3d:["$","h3",null,{"children":"Camera off? The renderer doesn’t care"}]
3e:["$","p",null,{"children":["A key constraint was that the piece stays alive — and generative — with no camera. So the renderer is ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"source-agnostic"}],": a procedural ",["$","code",null,{"children":"SyntheticSource"}]," feeds the exact same array layers the camera would. It is a three-stage chain:"]}]
3f:["$","ol",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Splat"}]," — a persistent texture, faded slightly every frame, then additively inked with one soft blob per live Lorenz deposit. A self-portrait of the attractor, in feedback."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Colourise"}]," — the splat is sampled through a ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"domain warp"}]," driven by 4-octave ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"fractional Brownian motion"}]," (fBm), then mapped through an ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Iñigo Quílez cosine palette"}],", the hue drifting off the live Lorenz ",["$","code",null,{"children":"z"}],", the audio centroid and a slow low-frequency oscillator (LFO)."]}],"\n"]}]
40:["$","p",null,{"children":"Here, fBm means “stack several layers of noise”: each octave is twice as fine and half as strong as the previous one. One layer looks like smooth randomness; four layers start to feel like natural turbulence."}]

44:["$","aside",null,{"className":"my-6 rounded-md border p-4 text-sm leading-6 border-blue-500/30 bg-blue-500/5","children":[["$","p",null,{"className":"mb-2 font-semibold text-foreground","children":"A note on lineage: the demoscene, in a browser tab"}],["$","div",null,{"className":"[&>:first-child]:mt-0 [&>:last-child]:mb-0","children":["$","p",null,{"children":["Hand-coded close to the metal, every pixel made by math instead of assets, synced to music in real time, the whole thing a flex of what the hardware can do — that is the ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"demoscene"}]," ethos, the 1980s–90s subculture of Amiga and PC groups coaxing impossible real-time audiovisuals out of bare silicon. Lorenz Clash wears the lineage openly: the starfield is rebuilt procedurally (zero assets), the camera-off visuals are pure noise and feedback, and even the colour comes from ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Iñigo Quílez’s cosine palette"}]," — IQ being a demoscene veteran whose ",["$","code",null,{"children":"a + b·cos(2π(c·t + d))"}]," trick is now standard procedural-graphics vocabulary. Swap the Amiga for a phone GPU and the assembly for WGSL, and the spirit is the same."]}]}]]}]
45:["$","h3",null,{"children":"The frame, pass by pass"}]
46:["$","p",null,{"children":"Everything happens inside one command encoder, one submit. Almost all of the visual work is render pipelines — every particle effect is computed analytically in a vertex shader over instanced cubes. The only compute pass in the shipped app is a tiny iOS camera-copy probe that scans for pure-black edge bands before the frame is stored. The order:"}]
47:["$","ol",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Capture passes"}]," — write the camera (or synthetic) frames into ring-buffer layers. Must come first, since the scene samples them."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Trail passes"}]," — a half-res persistent buffer is faded and re-inked, for smoke-like smear."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Scene pass"}]," (depth-tested, into an offscreen target when bloom is on): starfield dome → deformation grid → ribbons and morphing shapes (curve A, then curve B rotated) → comets and their wakes → tail-dissolution particles → the head crest."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Bloom"}]," — the post chain."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Blit"}]," — present."]}],"\n"]}]
48:["$","$L3",null,{"lightSrc":"/images/2026/lorenz-clash/diagram-frame-pipeline-light-v7.png","darkSrc":"/images/2026/lorenz-clash/diagram-frame-pipeline-light-v7.png","alt":"One WebGPU frame: capture into the texture-array ring buffer, update the persistent trail, render the scene offscreen, bloom it, then copy the owned present texture to the canvas and export path.","width":1650,"height":941}]
49:["$","p",null,{"children":"A quick tour of what lives in that scene pass:"}]
4a:["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Travelers / comets"}]," — a cube and a sphere ride each curve along a Catmull-Rom spline, spiralling in the plane perpendicular to the tangent (in phase opposition), trailing a helical ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"wake"}],"."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Shape morph"}]," — a head-to-tail wave that turns the ribbon into cubes, then spheres, as a ",["$","em",null,{"children":"geometric"}]," cross-fade rather than an alpha blend (the incoming form grows from the head while the outgoing shrinks)."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Starfield"}]," — a procedural dome reconstructed from the camera basis, so the stars rotate correctly as the camera orbits. Zero assets."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Head crest"}]," — additive cubes riding the newest deposit on an audio-reactive sine wave: the visible “now” of the ribbon."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Deformation grid"}]," — a fBm-displaced floor lattice, normally subtle, but sometimes hit by accelerating rainbow wave fronts on rhythmic cues."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Key-frame glow"}]," — when a tile corresponds to a captured high-definition (HD) still, its deposit carries a flag and pulses with a desynchronised colour accent."]}],"\n"]}]

55:["$","p",null,{"children":["Two ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"follow"}]," modes trade the orbit for a ride along the curve. 5d:["$","p",null,{"children":["That slow-motion ripple later became its own effect. The ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"pixel ripple"}]," uses the same composite pass, but with a separate event uniform: when a roll, snare or strong kick lands, the app launches a short radial wave with randomized amount, duration, frequency and speed. The randomness matters. A fixed ripple looks like a canned transition after three plays; a bounded range makes it feel like the music is throwing pressure waves through the scene. If the score is quiet, a sparse Poisson fallback can still trigger one, so the effect is music-timed without depending on the auto-director being enabled."]}]
5e:["$","p",null,{"children":["The more expensive-looking effect is actually the simplest one conceptually: an ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"exposure trail"}],", like leaving a camera shutter open for a few seconds. After the final composite, a tiny temporal-feedback pass mixes the current image with a decayed copy of the previous output in two owned ping-pong textures. It fades in, holds, fades out, and never reads the live swapchain. There are two timings: short hits of about ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"1.5 s"}],", usually around cuts or strong rhythmic events, and long trails of about ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"20 s"}]," for calmer floats, bridges and breakdowns. The counts scale with song length: at four minutes the cap is ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"20 short"}]," and ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"3 long"}]," plays, with shorter or longer tracks scaled proportionally. Like the ripples, it is score-driven but independent of the camera director — turning off auto-camera should not turn off the visual life of the music."]}]
5f:["$","p",null,{"children":"It is a good miniature of the whole compositing philosophy: fold the effect into the pass that already touches every pixel, or into a single owned post pass when temporal history is needed, and keep the renderer’s layer count under control."}]

Reading from ",["$","code",null,{"children":"getCurrentTexture()"}]," directly — the obvious thing — stalls and corrupts presentation on iOS Safari. The owned-texture detour also gives video export a stable surface to grab, without ever touching the live swapchain."]}]}]]}]
61:["$","h3",null,{"children":"The audio-reactive layer"}]
62:["$","p",null,{"children":["Audio is an ",["$","code",null,{"children":"AnalyserNode"}]," with a Fast Fourier transform (FFT) size of 2048, tapped ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"before"}]," the master gain, so muting the music silences your ears but keeps the visuals dancing. Each frame it extracts level as root mean square (RMS), bass/mid/treble (mean linear amplitude over Hz bands, normalized against offline-measured percentiles), a log-mapped spectral ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"centroid"}],", and a ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"beat"}]," estimate (bass flux above a slow running average — fast attack, slow decay)."]}]
63:["$","p",null,{"children":"Those features drive three separate parts of the system:"}]
64:["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Live and global"}],", packed into the shared camera uniform — driving the head crest, edge tints, bloom flashes and parameter modulation right now."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Frozen per deposit"}]," — the snapshot baked into each ribbon tile at birth. This is what makes the ribbon a recording: each tile keeps the ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"color"}]," (centroid → palette, on the edges only), ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"size"}]," (bass + beat → grow) and ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"spin"}]," (treble) of the instant it was created, even as the music moves on."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Transport time"}]," — the slow-mo gesture produces a smoothed ",["$","code",null,{"children":"warp"}]," from 1.0 down to about 0.35. That same number slows the music, the Lorenz scroll, the deposit rate, the comet motion and the composite ripple, so the tape-stop reads as one event instead of five unrelated effects."]}],"\n"]}]
65:["$","p",null,{"children":["The mapping is deliberately small enough to stay legible. ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Level plus beat"}]," push ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"ρ"}]," and scroll speed, which makes the attractor feel like it is breathing with the kick. 67:["$","h3",null,{"children":"From FFT to a score: offline music structure"}]
68:["$","p",null,{"children":["The live FFT is good at ",["$","em",null,{"children":"now"}],": how loud, how bright, how much bass, whether something just attacked. It is not good at ",["$","em",null,{"children":"where we are in the song"}],". An intro, a breakdown, a drive section and a floating bridge can have similar instantaneous energy for a few seconds, but they ask for different camera language. An intro wants a wide orbit. A driving section can tolerate follow shots, rapid cuts and comets. A calm bridge is where a long exposure trail feels earned."]}]

6b:["$","p",null,{"children":["For each bundled ",["$","code",null,{"children":".m4a"}],", it resamples to ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"22.05 kHz"}],", computes onset strength, tempo and beat times, then derives RMS, spectral centroid, chroma and Mel-frequency cepstral coefficient (MFCC) features on a one-second grid. A novelty curve compares the local feature profile before and after each time point (an eight-second context on each side), peaks become candidate section boundaries, and each section gets a coarse role: ",["$","code",null,{"children":"intro"}],", ",["$","code",null,{"children":"drive"}],", ",["$","code",null,{"children":"groove"}],", ",["$","code",null,{"children":"break"}],", ",["$","code",null,{"children":"bridge"}],", ",["$","code",null,{"children":"float"}]," or ",["$","code",null,{"children":"outro"}],"."]}]
6c:["$","p",null,{"children":["The same pass extracts rhythmic cues in separate bands: low-band flux for ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"kicks"}],", high-band flux for ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"snares"}],", mid-band flux for ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"toms"}],", and short dense snare sequences for ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"rolls"}],". Across the 11 tracks, the current JSON contains ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"69 sections"}],", ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"4,875 beats"}],", ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"2,966 kicks"}],", ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"2,998 snares"}],", ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"1,408 toms"}]," and ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"115 rolls"}]," — about ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"42 minutes"}]," of pre-analysed timing, still with no server and no runtime machine learning (ML)."]}]

6f:["$","$L3",null,{"lightSrc":"/images/2026/lorenz-clash/diagram-offline-music-score-light-v1.png","darkSrc":"/images/2026/lorenz-clash/diagram-offline-music-score-light-v1.png","alt":"The offline music score pipeline: local tracks are analysed with a uv Python script and librosa, resampled to 22.05 kHz, converted into features, section roles and rhythmic events, committed as JSON, then used by the runtime director to trigger camera and visual effect cues.","width":1672,"height":941}]
70:["$","p",null,{"children":["There are two directors now. The original one is still there: a classic live-FFT novelty detector that compares a short-term profile against a long-term one and switches when the sound drifts far enough. The structured director sits beside it, unchanged by the live detector. When playback enters a new analysed section, it applies the section’s preset; when beats, snares, toms and rolls pass the playhead, it emits small cues that can trigger ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"zoom pulses"}],", ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"rapid camera jumps"}],", ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"comets"}],", ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"grid waves"}],", ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"pixel ripples"}]," and ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"exposure trails"}],". The colour, grow and shimmer still come from the live FFT, so the score never freezes the performance — it just gives the system a map."]}]
71:["$","p",null,{"children":"That separation matters. You can turn the camera director off and still keep the score-driven effects: the music can keep throwing ripples and exposure moments at the renderer without taking over your view. It also keeps the experience from feeling like a fixed music video. Section changes are deterministic anchors, but the micro-events keep probability, cooldowns and random ranges, so the same track has a recognisable structure without replaying the exact same cuts every time."}]
72:["$","aside",null,{"className":"my-6 rounded-md border p-4 text-sm leading-6 border-blue-500/30 bg-blue-500/5","children":[["$","p",null,{"className":"mb-2 font-semibold text-foreground","children":"War story: iOS broke the obvious slow-mo"}],["$","div",null,{"className":"[&>:first-child]:mt-0 [&>:last-child]:mb-0","children":["$","p",null,{"children":["The obvious implementation is ",["$","code",null,{"children":"audioElement.playbackRate = warp"}],". It works until that element is routed through ",["$","code",null,{"children":"createMediaElementSource()"}]," on iOS, where changing the rate can cut or re-buffer the sound. The workaround is heavier but stable: decode the current track ahead of time, switch to an ",["$","code",null,{"children":"AudioBufferSourceNode"}]," when ",["$","code",null,{"children":"warp < 0.99"}],", drive that node’s ",["$","code",null,{"children":"playbackRate"}],", and feed it into the same analyser. Returning to normal is just ",["$","code",null,{"children":"rate → 1"}]," — no seek, no restart. The original ",["$","code",null,{"children":"<audio>"}]," element only takes over again on the next track."]}]}]]}]
73:["$","p",null,{"children":["And one honest note on the music itself: every track is ",["$","strong",null,{"children":["original Goa trance, generated with ",["$","a",null,{"href":"https://suno.com","children":"Suno"}]]}]," and encoded to 192 kbps Advanced Audio Coding (AAC). 7f:["$","p",null,{"children":["The hardware encoder already runs off-thread, so no Web Worker is needed — the main thread is barely involved. 85:["$","p",null,{"children":["The audio in the export isn’t a recording of the output — it’s the ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"actual track"}]," that was playing, re-decoded from the local ",["$","code",null,{"children":".m4a"}],", sliced to each clip’s window and laid end-to-end with ~10 ms boundary fades so the joins don’t click. 86:["$","aside",null,{"className":"my-6 rounded-md border p-4 text-sm leading-6 border-blue-500/30 bg-blue-500/5","children":[["$","p",null,{"className":"mb-2 font-semibold text-foreground","children":"War story: decode with an OfflineAudioContext, never a real one"}],["$","div",null,{"className":"[&>:first-child]:mt-0 [&>:last-child]:mb-0","children":["$","p",null,{"children":["Decoding the track needs an ",["$","code",null,{"children":"AudioContext"}]," — but creating a ",["$","em",null,{"children":"real"}]," one grabs the hardware audio session, and on iOS that ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"suspends the live music’s context"}],", silencing the app until a reload; every export or preview tap would kill the sound. And since decoding a full multi-minute track is by far the heaviest step, the most-recently-decoded track is cached — but only ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"one"}]," entry, because a decoded 8-minute stereo track at 48 kHz is ~180 MB and holding two would OOM."]}]}]]}]
87:["$","p",null,{"children":["When you pull the visuals into slow-motion, the sound has to slow with them — so each recorded frame stores its slow-mo ",["$","code",null,{"children":"warp"}],", and the export ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"resamples the music along that envelope"}],": the read head advances more slowly through the samples exactly where the video was tape-stopped, with linear interpolation of the now-fractional position. 89:["$","h2",null,{"children":"Surviving it: the iPad that ran out of GPU"}]
8a:["$","p",null,{"children":["It ran beautifully on an iPhone 13 and an iPhone SE — then crashed an ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"iPad Pro 2018"}]," after a few minutes. The reflex is “old device, less memory,” but that iPad has the ",["$","em",null,{"children":"same"}]," 4 GB as the phones, or more. What it has that they don’t is a much ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"bigger screen"}]," and, that day, the camera held in ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"landscape"}],". Both mattered, and chasing why is the most instructive part of the build."]}]
8b:["$","p",null,{"children":["Safari’s remote Web Inspector was useful while the page was alive, but it was not enough for the failure itself: once the GPU process disappeared, the useful state had to already be visible on the device. So the app grew a ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"diagnostics line"}]," — printed every ten seconds and ",["$","em",null,{"children":"baked onto the crash screen itself"}]," — reporting frame rate, clip count, encoder count and the total bytes of every texture it had allocated. A screenshot of the crash became a full readout."]}]
8c:["$","aside",null,{"className":"my-6 rounded-md border p-4 text-sm leading-6 border-blue-500/30 bg-blue-500/5","children":[["$","p",null,{"className":"mb-2 font-semibold text-foreground","children":"War story: it ran out of GPU memory, not RAM — and iOS won't say"}],["$","div",null,{"className":"[&>:first-child]:mt-0 [&>:last-child]:mb-0","children":["$","p",null,{"children":["The crash was always a GPU allocation failing — ",["$","code",null,{"children":"beginRenderPass"}]," or ",["$","code",null,{"children":"importExternalTexture"}]," returning nothing — never a JavaScript out-of-memory. WebKit’s ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"GPU process"}]," has its own budget, separate from the page heap, and a big screen plus a live camera fills it fast. Worse, ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"iOS exposes no memory API"}]," at all (",["$","code",null,{"children":"deviceMemory"}],", ",["$","code",null,{"children":"performance.memory"}],", ",["$","code",null,{"children":"measureUserAgentSpecificMemory"}]," are Chrome-only) and WebGPU reports no video memory (VRAM) — you fly blind. And once that process dies, ",["$","code",null,{"children":"requestAdapter()"}]," returns ",["$","code",null,{"children":"null"}],": the whole subsystem is gone, so there is no recovering in place, only a reload."]}]}]]}]
8d:["$","p",null,{"children":["The biggest single lever was the ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"ring buffer"}],". Its layers are sized to the camera’s aspect ratio, and a landscape frame holds about ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"three times"}]," the pixels of a portrait one — so on the landscape iPad the ring alone was ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"248 of 288 MB"}],". Capping each layer’s ",["$","em",null,{"children":"longer"}]," edge instead of its height makes the footprint orientation-independent: 288 MB became ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"125 MB"}],", and the already-small portrait phones were untouched."]}]
8e:["$","aside",null,{"className":"my-6 rounded-md border p-4 text-sm leading-6 border-blue-500/30 bg-blue-500/5","children":[["$","p",null,{"className":"mb-2 font-semibold text-foreground","children":"War story: one encoder, reset between clips"}],["$","div",null,{"className":"[&>:first-child]:mt-0 [&>:last-child]:mb-0","children":["$","p",null,{"children":["The recorder first built a fresh ",["$","code",null,{"children":"VideoEncoder"}]," per clip. On iOS that churns ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"VideoToolbox sessions"}],", and after a dozen or two the next one fails and takes the GPU process with it. The fix is ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"one"}]," encoder for the whole session, ",["$","code",null,{"children":"reset()"}]," between clips — which quietly fixed two more bugs: reusing an encoder across clips with each clip’s timestamps restarting at zero had been feeding it ",["$","em",null,{"children":"backward"}]," time jumps (corrupt, frozen frames), and a shared encoder emits its ",["$","code",null,{"children":"decoderConfig"}]," only once, so every clip after the first was muxed with none and wouldn’t open. A clean reset makes each clip an independent, well-formed encode."]}]}]]}]
8f:["$","p",null,{"children":["The leak that set the ceiling was the camera. ",["$","code",null,{"children":"importExternalTexture()"}]," is minted fresh on demand and iOS reclaims those transient external textures slowly. The obvious fix — copy the frame once into a texture I own and stop importing — is exactly what worked in the end, but it first broke in the most iOS way possible."]}]
90:["$","aside",null,{"className":"my-6 rounded-md border p-4 text-sm leading-6 border-blue-500/30 bg-blue-500/5","children":[["$","p",null,{"className":"mb-2 font-semibold text-foreground","children":"War story: the black rectangle detector, then the square stream"}],["$","div",null,{"className":"[&>:first-child]:mt-0 [&>:last-child]:mb-0","children":[["$","p",null,{"children":["Swapping ",["$","code",null,{"children":"importExternalTexture"}]," for ",["$","code",null,{"children":"copyExternalImageToTexture"}]," into an owned texture removed the slow iPad leak, then rendered the iPhone camera as a stretched image with a pure-black side rectangle. Hard-coding a crop fixed one phone orientation and broke another. The first real breakthrough was a tiny GPU probe: scan the copied frame at full resolution, count edge rows and columns that are pure black, ignore all-black startup frames, take three samples, then crop and recompute the visible aspect ratio before the ribbon stores the image."]}],["$","p",null,{"children":["The final fix was even better: on Apple mobile, request the camera as a ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"square stream"}]," (",["$","code",null,{"children":"720×720"}],", aspect ",["$","code",null,{"children":"1"}],"). Lorenz Clash uses the camera as square material anyway, and this nudges WebKit into returning a centered, already-usable frame. The black-rectangle detector stays in place as a diagnostic and fallback, but the happy path now logs ",["$","code",null,{"children":"track 720x720 aspect=1.000"}]," and ",["$","code",null,{"children":"copyCrop=none"}],". iOS/iPadOS use this owned copy path; desktop and Android keep the simpler external-texture path."]}]]}]]}]
91:["$","p",null,{"children":["There was also a cheap win before that: ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"only touch the camera on frames that actually capture"}]," a ribbon deposit. Deposits arrive irregularly, so the in-between frames had been minting textures for nothing. That reduced the leak while the copy-path work was still unstable, and it remains useful because it lowers camera work on every device."]}]
92:["$","p",null,{"children":["Export, on a tight device, is both victim and trigger — and the two fixes are the same idea twice: ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"react, don’t measure"}]," (you can’t measure). With no memory API to size the export to the device, the encoder’s own ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"faults"}]," are the signal — each failure drops the export resolution a notch and retries, so a capable machine stays at full resolution while a GPU-tight one ratchets down to something sustainable. And a device that can’t hold 30 fps during capture drops frames: timestamping by frame ",["$","em",null,{"children":"count"}]," exported a 5-second take as a shorter, sped-up clip, so frames are now stamped by ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"real elapsed time"}],", keeping the duration honest at the device’s true rate."]}]
93:["$","p",null,{"children":["The last fix was a policy. Background clips had been a ",["$","em",null,{"children":"rolling buffer"}]," — evict the oldest at the cap, keep encoding — which means the hardware encoder runs ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"continuously"}]," for as long as the app is open, and that sustained load is what finally tips a tight device over. So auto-capture now ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"pauses"}]," at the cap instead, and a small curation user interface (UI) — keep, trash, or “clear unkept” — frees slots to resume. Don’t encode forever just to throw it away."]}]
94:["$","p",null,{"children":["The result: continuous camera-and-capture went from a crash at ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"~5 minutes"}]," to ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"past thirty"}]," on the same iPad, GPU memory flat throughout. The final iOS copy path now logs the square camera stream (",["$","code",null,{"children":"track 720x720 aspect=1.000"}],") and removes the ",["$","code",null,{"children":"importExternalTexture"}]," counter from the long run (",["$","code",null,{"children":"camImp=0"}],", ",["$","code",null,{"children":"camCopy"}]," grows at the deposit rate). The iPad can still get hot — this is a 2018 tablet running WebGPU, camera and video encoding in a browser — but the failure mode changed from a slow GPU-memory cliff to ordinary thermal/performance pressure. That is the difference between a demo that dies and an experience I can ship."]}]
95:["$","h2",null,{"children":"Shipping it: a fullscreen PWA"}]
96:["$","p",null,{"children":["A ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Progressive Web App"}]," (PWA) is a website that the browser can treat more like an app: it can be added to the home screen, get its own icon, launch in a standalone or fullscreen window, and cache enough of itself to open reliably. For Lorenz Clash, the important part is not offline mode; it is ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"immersion"}],". The piece needs to escape the browser chrome, especially on mobile, so the camera canvas can fill the screen like an installed app."]}]
97:["$","p",null,{"children":["That installable shape comes from two small web primitives: a ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"web app manifest"}],", which describes the app’s name, icons, colors and display mode; and a ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"service worker"}],", which lets the browser recognise that the site has an app shell it can control. Chrome on desktop and Android supports the full install flow from the browser UI. On iOS and iPadOS, install it from Safari: open the site, tap Share, then ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Add to Home Screen"}],"."]}]
98:["$","$L3",null,{"lightSrc":"/images/2026/lorenz-clash/install-safari-ipad-add-to-home-screen.png","darkSrc":"/images/2026/lorenz-clash/install-safari-ipad-add-to-home-screen.png","alt":"Installing Lorenz Clash on iPad: Safari's Share menu opens the Add to Home Screen dialog, previewing the app icon and name with Open as Web App enabled for a fullscreen launch.","width":2732,"height":2048}]
